Sooo... I saw a clip of this on Insta and somewhere in this Margot Robbie said that a producer on Oppenheimer asked to move Barbie's release date. Robbie got back at him saying if he's scared, Oppenheimer should move. Neither of them did. Cillian Murphy called it "good instinct" on her part.  Here's the thing, Oppenheimer got the date first. WB set Barbie on the same day specifically to spite Nolan after he felt betrayed over their streaming decision with HBOMax. Oppenheimer is a 3 hour, R rated historical biopic. Of course the producer was scared â€” Barbie is a 2 hours IP-based fantasy comedy in PG13. It *would've* crush Oppenheimer.  As previously said, neither of them moved. It was Pink vs Black. But... there was an appeal to this. The people found it amusing enough and the phenomenon grew. It no longer became a "versus", it was a pair. It was a "date". We decided that Pink and Black go well together.  Admittedly, this is a very minor thing. I watched Barbie the other day at the request of my sister. I understood the point the movie was trying to convey (that the patriarchy is bad for both sexes, correct me if I'm wrong), but I don't think it did it very well. Perhaps that's why Barbie was seen as somewhat divisive. I think the section in the movie that highlighted that the patriarchy is bad for men was more rushed, thus diminishing its importantance. Almost like it was a footnote or an afterthought. Similarly, with the quip at the end regarding corporations not really caring about anything as long as they make money. It kind of felt as though the movie was too focussed on making a statement at the expense of the story. Personally I'm of the view that well-written movies put the story first and the message is more implicit thus giving the opportunity to the viewer to consider their own thoughts on the matter after watching rather than the opinions of the writer being so apparent. Ultimately I think they did a disservice to the cause they were trying to bring attention to, as demonstrated by how divisive the comments were on the film afterwards.

It always amazes me how actors have an incredible blind spot for how inane their movies really are/were. First of all, not impressed with Oppenheimer whatsoever. Spectacularly talented cast, lackluster script, and everything bouncing around in time served no actual purpose but to confuse the viewer. There was no reason (and there just usually isn't any)  for the director to break up the flow of a story that way. The reason they do it, is to try to make an otherwise lifeless plot more interesting. I don't like this technique in most movies and it definitely didn't work here. The most unconvincing part of Murphy's Oppenheimer was the way he never seemed to really get pissed off by the way the government betrayed him and belittled his contributions. Was not convinced.  Barbie, on the other hand, almost needs no commentary whatsoever. Why would an adult actually want to SEE a movie like this in the first place? Even Margot Robbie, who has exhibited some depth and talent as an actress in other roles, could not possibly save a wretched, juvenile role such as this. Then again, she's played bombastic, over the top characters before, so I guess that's her chosen career path now. Compare her with another Aussie actress, Naomi Watts, and there is really NO comparison between Robbie's roles and the depths of the women played by Watts, who is a STUNNING actress and has chosen roles with much more depth, purpose and character. Just another day in the fog of Hollyweird, folks.
